Automatically classifies tasks into compliance tiers and enforces appropriate verification.\n\n**Key Benefits**:\n- Single command replaces confusion between `sc:task` and `sc:task-mcp`\n- Automatic tier classification with confidence scoring\n- Appropriate verification for each task type\n- Prevents over-engineering for trivial changes\n- Ensures safety for critical changes\n\n## Triggers\n\nUse `/sc:task` when:\n- Task involves code modifications with downstream impacts\n- Complexity score >0.6 with code modifications\n- Multi-file scope (>2 estimated affected files)\n- Security domain paths detected (auth/, security/, crypto/)\n- Refactoring or system-wide changes requested\n\n**Auto-Suggest Keywords**:\n- High confidence: \"implement feature\", \"refactor system\", \"fix security\", \"add authentication\", \"update database schema\"\n- Moderate confidence: \"add new\", \"create component\", \"update service\", \"modify API\"\n\n## Usage\n\n```bash\n/sc:task [description]                           # Auto-detect all dimensions\n/sc:task [description] --compliance strict       # Force STRICT tier\n/sc:task [description] --compliance light        # Force LIGHT tier\n/sc:task [description] --skip-compliance         # Bypass compliance (escape hatch)\n/sc:task [description] --verify auto             # Auto-select verification\n```\n\n## Behavioral Flow\n\n### 0. Classification (Already Performed)\n\nClassification was handled by the `/sc:task` command before this skill was invoked. The tier has been determined and the classification header has been emitted. Proceed directly to execution based on the classified tier.\n\n**Reference** — the tier keyword tables (for context only, do not re-classify):\n- **STRICT**: security, authentication, database, migration, refactor, breaking change, encrypt, token, session, oauth\n- **EXEMPT**: explain, search, commit, push, plan, discuss, brainstorm\n- **LIGHT**: typo, comment, whitespace, lint, docstring, formatting, minor\n- **STANDARD**: implement, add, create, update, fix, build, modify, change (default)\n\n### 2. Override with: `--compliance [strict|standard|light|exempt]`\"\n\n**Note**: The machine-readable header (Section 0) is for telemetry/A/B testing. This human-readable display is for user understanding.\n\n### 3. Execution Phase\n\nExecute task according to tier requirements:\n\n**STRICT Execution**:\n1. Activate project (mcp__serena__activate_project)\n2. Verify git working directory clean (git status)\n3. Load codebase context (codebase-retrieval)\n4. Check relevant memories (list_memories -> read_memory)\n5. Identify all affected files and test files\n6. Make changes with full checklist\n7. Identify all files that import changed code\n8. Update all affected files\n9. Spawn verification agent (quality-engineer)\n10. Run comprehensive tests: `pytest [path] -v`\n11. Answer adversarial questions\n\n**STANDARD Execution**:\n1. Load context via codebase-retrieval\n2. Search downstream impacts (find_referencing_symbols OR grep)\n3. Make changes\n4. Run affected tests OR document manual verification\n5. Verify basic functionality\n\n**LIGHT Execution**:\n1. Quick scope check (files/lines within bounds)\n2. Make changes\n3. Quick sanity check (syntax valid, no obvious errors)\n4. Proceed with judgment\n\n**EXEMPT Execution**:\n1. Execute immediately\n2. No verification overhead\n\n### 4. Verification Phase\n\nRoute to appropriate verification based on tier and paths:\n\n| Compliance Tier | Verification Method | Token Cost | Timeout |\n|-----------------|---------------------|------------|---------|\n| STRICT | Sub-agent (quality-engineer) | 3-5K | 60s |\n| STANDARD | Direct test execution | 300-500 | 30s |\n| LIGHT | Skip verification | 0 | 0s |\n| EXEMPT | Skip verification | 0 | 0s |\n\n**Critical Path Override**: Paths matching `auth/`, `security/`, `crypto/`, `models/`, `migrations/` always trigger CRITICAL verification regardless of compliance tier.\n\n**Trivial Path Override**: Paths matching `*.md`, `docs/`, `*test*.py` may skip verification.\n\n### 5. Feedback Collection\n\nAfter completion, collect implicit feedback:\n- Track if user overrode tier (implicit classification feedback)\n- Note smooth completion vs errors (quality signal)\n- Store for calibration learning\n\n## MCP Integration\n\n**Required Servers by Tier**:\n- STRICT: Sequential, Serena (fallback not allowed)\n- STANDARD: Sequential, Context7 (fallback allowed)\n- LIGHT: None required (fallback allowed)\n- EXEMPT: None required\n\n**Circuit Breaker Behavior**:\n- If required servers unavailable for STRICT tier, block task execution\n- For other tiers, use fallbacks with noted limitations\n\n## Tool Coordination\n\n**Planning Phase**:\n1. TodoWrite: Create task breakdown\n2. codebase-retrieval: Load context\n3. list_memories / read_memory: Check project state\n\n**Execution Phase**:\n1. Edit/MultiEdit/Write: Make changes\n2. Grep/Glob: Find references\n3. find_referencing_symbols: Trace dependencies\n\n**Verification Phase**:\n1. Task (quality-engineer): Spawn verification agent (STRICT only)\n2. Bash: Run tests directly (STANDARD)\n3. think_about_task_adherence: Reflect on completeness\n\n**Completion Phase**:\n1. write_memory: Save session state\n2. think_about_whether_you_are_done: Final check\n\n## Examples\n\n### STRICT Task\n```\n/sc:task \"implement user authentication with JWT\"\n\n-> Classified as STRICT (security domain, authentication keyword)\n-> Full 6-category checklist classification\n-> Full verification enforced\n```\n\n## Boundaries\n\n**Will:**\n- Classify tasks into appropriate compliance tiers\n- Enforce tier-appropriate verification requirements\n- Provide \"\"\"Signal 2: Independent no-error-path detection.\n   223→\n   224→    Computation returns value on degenerate input without exception = potential silent corruption.\n   225→    Works even without   }\n   240→    is_degenerate = domain.category in degenerate_categories\n   241→\n   242→    if has_error_path:\n   243→        # Explicit error handling -> immediate detection\n   244→ phases (M1->P1, M2->P2, M3->P3, M4->P4)\n    54→- Phase numbering: contiguous 1-4 with no gaps\n    55→- Task ID scheme: T<PP>.<TT> zero-padded (e.g., T01.03)\n    56→- Task conversion: each implement/verify deliverable pair (D.x.a + D.x.b) -> 1 task; integration deliverables -> 1 task each\n    57→- Checkpoint cadence: after every 5 tasks + end of each phase\n    58→- Clarification task rule: no clarification tasks needed (roadmap is fully specified)\n    59→- Deliverable registry: D-0001 through D-0048 in task appearance order\n    60→- Effort mapping: computed from text length, keywords (schema, migration, performance), split status, dependency words\n    61→- Risk mapping: computed from security/data/auth/performance/cross-cutting keywords\n    62→- Tier classification: keyword scoring + context boosters; most tasks STRICT due to schema/state/mutation content\n    63→- Verification routing: STRICT -> sub-agent (quality-engineer), STANDARD -> direct test execution\n Guard pipeline pass\n\n### `/config/workspace/SuperClaude_Framework/src/superclaude/cli/pipeline/guard_pass.py`\n\nThis is implemented.\n\nKey dataclass:\n#### `GuardAnalysisOutput`\n```python\ndetections: list[GuardDetection]\nresolution: GuardResolutionOutput\ninvariant_cross_refs: dict[str, InvariantEntry | None]\nfmea_elevations: list[str]\nsection_markdown: str\n```\n\nProperty:\n- `can_advance_to_m4`\n\nPrimary API:\n#### `run_guard_analysis_pass(...)`\n```python\ndef run_guard_analysis_pass(\n    deliverables: list[Deliverable],\n    invariant_output: InvariantRegistryOutput | None = None,\n    fmea_severity_map: dict[str, str] | None = None,\n) -> GuardAnalysisOutput:\n```\n\nInternal helpers:\n- `_cross_reference_invariants(...)`\n- `_check_fmea_elevation(...)`\n- `_render_empty_section()`\n- `_render_guard_analysis_section(...)`\n\n### How M3 currently integrates with M2\nIt expects:\n- all deliverables\n- `InvariantRegistryOutput` from M2\n- a reduced `fmea_severity_map`\n\nM3 then:\n1. runs guard detection\n2. cross-references guard variables against invariant entries\n3. checks whether ambiguous guards should be elevated based on FMEA severity\n4. resolves guards into `GUARD_TEST` deliverables and gate warnings\n5. renders markdown\n\n### Important implementation note\n`_check_fmea_elevation(...)` uses string severities and only elevates for:\n- `\"high\"`\n- `\"critical\"`\n\nBut M2 `Severity.value` is:\n- `\"data_loss\"`\n- `\"wrong_state\"`\n- `\"degraded\"`\n- `\"cosmetic\"`\n\nSo there is a semantic mismatch between current M2 enum values and M3 elevation input expectations. This is the most important integration issue I found.\n\nIf you hook M3 directly to M2 today, you need a mapping layer, otherwise elevation will not trigger correctly from raw `Severity.value`.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Key integration points for Phase 3 hook-up\n\nIf you are wiring M3 after M2, the contract should be:\n\n1. Run:\n   - `run_combined_m2_pass(deliverables, ...)`\n\n2. Build FMEA severity map from:\n   - `CombinedM2Output.failure_modes`\n\n3. Pass to:\n   - `run_guard_analysis_pass(deliverables + maybe_generated?, invariant_output, fmea_severity_map)`\n\n### Inputs M3 needs\n- `deliverables: list[Deliverable]`\n- `invariant_output: InvariantRegistryOutput`\n- `fmea_severity_map: dict[str, str]`\n\n### Outputs M3 produces\n- `GuardAnalysisOutput.detections`\n- `GuardAnalysisOutput.resolution.guard_test_deliverables`\n- `GuardAnalysisOutput.resolution.gate_warnings`\n- `GuardAnalysisOutput.section_markdown`\n- `GuardAnalysisOutput.can_advance_to_m4`\n\n### Likely required adapter\nBecause of the severity mismatch:\n- M2 severity enum values: `data_loss`, `wrong_state`, `degraded`, `cosmetic`\n- M3 elevation expects: `high`, `critical`\n\nYou likely need a mapping such as:\n- `data_loss -> critical`\n- `wrong_state -> high`\n- `degraded -> medium/low`\n- `cosmetic -> low`\n\nWithout that adapter, `fmea_elevations` may stay empty even when M2 found serious failures.\n\n---\n\n## 11.    - Guard has ambiguity\n    - Source deliverable has FMEA severity >= \"high\"\n    \"\"\"\n    elevations: list[str] = []\n    high_severities = {\"high\", \"critical\"}\n\n    for detection in _render_guard_analysis_section(\n    detections: list[GuardDetection],\n    resolution: GuardResolutionOutput,\n    invariant_cross_refs: dict[str, InvariantEntry | None],\n    fmea_elevations: list[str],\n) -> str:\n    \"\"\"Render the guard analysis section as markdown.\"\"\"\n    lines = [\"## Guard Analysis\", \"\"]\n    lines.append(f\"**Guards detected**: {len(detections)}\")\n    ambiguous_count = sum(1 for d in detections if d.has_ambiguity)\n    lines.append(f\"**Ambiguous guards**: {ambiguous_count}\")\n    lines.append(f\"**FMEA elevations**: {len(fmea_elevations)}\")\n    lines.append(\"\")\n\n    # State enumeration table\n    lines.append(\"### State Enumeration\")\n    lines.append(\"\")\n    lines.append(\"| Variable | Kind | States | Ambiguous | Invariant Registered | FMEA Elevated |\")\n    lines.append(\"|----------|------|--------|-----------|---------------------|---------------|\")\n    for det in detections:\n        states_str = \", \".join(s.value for s in det.states)\n        ambig = \"YES\" if det.has_ambiguity else \"no\"\n        inv_ref = invariant_cross_refs.get(det.guard_variable)\n        has_inv = \"YES\" if inv_ref else \"no\"\n        elevated = \"YES\" if det.guard_variable in fmea_elevations else \"no\"\n        lines.append(\n            f\"| `{det.guard_variable}` | {det.guard_kind.value} | {states_str} | \"\n            f\"{ambig} | {has_inv} | {elevated} |\"\n        )\n    lines.append(\"\")\n\n    # Append resolution section\n    if resolution.section_markdown:\n        lines.append(resolution.section_markdown)\n\n    # Gate status\n    if resolution.has_blocking_warnings:\n        lines.append(\"\")\n        lines.append(\"### Release Gate Rule 2: BLOCKING\")\n        lines.append(\"\")\n        lines.append(\"Pipeline cannot advance to M4. Unresolved guard ambiguity requires owner assignment.\")\n\n    return \"\\n\".join(lines)\n","numLines":201,"startLine":1,"totalLines":201}}}

false}` with single semantic meaning each\n- **SENTINEL_VALUE**: `{sentinel, normal}` with marker vs. range meanings\n- **IF_ELSE / EARLY_RETURN**: `{truthy, falsy}` based on condition\n- **TYPE_CHANGE (bool->int)**: `{0, N>0, N<0}` where 0 inherits dual semantics\n- **TYPE_CHANGE (bool->enum)**: `{state_A, state_B, state_C}` with migration mapping\n- **TYPE_CHANGE (enum->string)**: `{valid, empty, unknown}` string states\n\n## Ambiguity Flagging Criteria\n\nA guard state is **ambiguous** when its value maps to 2+ semantic meanings.\n\n**Always-ambiguous**: bool->int transition for value `0` (original false + zero numeric)\n\n**Never-ambiguous**: bool flags with clear true/false, enum with exhaustive match\n\n## Suppression\n\n`@no-ambiguity-check(rationale)` suppresses detection. Rationale is mandatory.\n\n## Known Archetypes (R-010)\n\n- **replay**: `{0: [no events, start offset], N>0: [offset into list]}` — seeded from `_replayed_event_offset` pattern\n- **boolean**: `{true: [active], false: [inactive]}` — baseline flag pattern\n\n## Implementation\n\n- File: `src/superclaude/cli/pipeline/guard_analyzer.py`\n- Exports: `detect_guards`, `GuardDetection`, `GuardKind`, `TypeTransitionKind`, `GuardState`, `SemanticMeaning`\n- NFR-007 compliant: no imports from sprint or roadmap modules\n","numLines":52,"startLine":1,"totalLines":52}}}
